## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: solid mechanics / materials science (thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling)
**Analysis**: The variables are stress (sigma), strain (epsilon), and temperature (T), which directly correspond to thermoelastic and thermoplastic constitutive relations in solid mechanics. Typical relationships include linear elasticity with temperature-dependent modulus, thermal strain offsets, nonlinear (hyperelastic) stress–strain laws, and temperature-driven softening of modulus or yield/flow stress.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke’s law (isothermal linear elasticity): sigma = c0 * epsilon (small-strain elastic regime)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (linear-in-T): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (elastic stiffness varies approximately linearly with temperature)
- Quadratic temperature dependence of modulus: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T + c2 * T**2) * epsilon (curvature in stiffness-vs-temperature)
- Thermoelastic strain offset (CTE-type): sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * T) (stress depends on mechanical strain after subtracting thermal expansion strain)
- Reference-temperature thermoelasticity: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * (T - c2)) (thermal strain measured from a stress-free reference temperature)
- Nonlinear elastic polynomial: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (geometric/material nonlinearity at larger strain)
- Power-law strain hardening: sigma = c0 * (Abs(epsilon) + c1)**c2 * Sign(epsilon) (plastic/elastic-plastic hardening with tension–compression sign handling)
- Rational softening with temperature: sigma = c0 * epsilon / (c1 + c2 * T) (effective modulus decreases with T via a stabilizing denominator offset)
- Exponential thermal softening of modulus: sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * T) * epsilon (stiffness changes approximately exponentially with temperature)
- Multiplicative separation (hardening × thermal softening): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 + c4 * exp(c5 * T)) (separable strain and temperature effects)
- Coefficients coupled to temperature (T-dependent hardening): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + (c2 + c3 * T) * epsilon**2 (temperature changes both linear and nonlinear stiffness terms)
- Neo-Hookean-like uniaxial form using stretch lambda=1+epsilon: sigma = c0 * ((1 + epsilon) - (1 + epsilon)**(-2)) (finite-strain hyperelastic structure; avoids simple polynomials at large strain)
- Thermally activated weakening with strain softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon * exp(c1 * epsilon) * exp(c2 * T) (captures combined strain-driven hardening/softening and temperature sensitivity)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Small-strain elastic regime → sigma approximately proportional to epsilon (linear term dominates at low |epsilon|).
- Thermal expansion offsets → use (epsilon - c*T) or (epsilon - c*(T-c0)) so zero-stress strain shifts with temperature (stress-free thermal strain).
- Stiffness typically decreases with increasing T in many solids → model E(T) with decreasing linear/quadratic trends or with rational forms like 1/(c0+c1*T).
- Yield/flow stress often decreases with T (thermal softening) → multiplicative temperature factor on an otherwise strain-hardening law.
- Strain hardening often follows a power-law in |epsilon| over a regime → Abs(epsilon)**n with Sign(epsilon) for tension/compression symmetry.
- Finite-strain behavior is better captured using stretch (1+epsilon) terms → expressions like (1+epsilon) and (1+epsilon)**(-k) to represent geometric nonlinearity and avoid runaway polynomials.
- Coupled T–epsilon effects → allow T-dependent coefficients on epsilon and epsilon**2 terms when temperature changes both modulus and nonlinearity.
- Avoid singularities near epsilon ≈ -1 in stretch-based forms → add small offsets (Abs(epsilon)+c0) or choose domains where (1+epsilon)>0.
